           <dt>&#x22d9; yajurveda </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;ved&#x00e1;</em> m. 'the sacrificial Veda', the collective body of sacred Mantras or texts which constitute the Yajur-veda (these Mantras, though often consisting of the prose Yajus, are frequently identical with the Mantras of the &#x1e5a;ig-veda, the Yajur-veda being only a sort of sacrificial prayer-book for ihe Adhvaryu priests formed out of the &#x1e5a;ig-veda, which had to be dissected and rearranged with additional texts for sacrificial purposes ; the most characteristic feature of the Yajur-veda is its division into two distinct collections of texts, the Taittir&#x012b;ya-sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101; and the V&#x0101;jasaneyi-sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101;, q.v. ; the former of which is also called K&#x1e5b;ish&#x1e47;a, i.e. 'Black', because in it the Sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101; and Br&#x0101;hmana portions are confused ; and the latter &#x015a;ukla, i.e. 'White', because in this, which is thought the more recent of the two recensions, the Sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101; is cleared from confusion with its Brahma&#x1e47;a and is as it were white or orderly ; the order of sacrifices, however, of both recensions is similar, two of the principal being the Dar&#x015b;a-p&#x016b;r&#x1e47;a-m&#x0101;sa or sacrifice to be performed at new and full moon, and the A&#x015b;va-medha or horse-sacrifice ; <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#cf">cf.</a> IW. 6 ; 245, n. 2) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Br">Br.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#G&#x1e5b;&#x015a;rS">G&#x1e5b;&#x015a;rS.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>-kriy&#x0101;svara-lak&#x1e63;a&#x1e47;a</em> n. <em>-ja&#x1e6d;&#x00e2;vali</em> f. <em>-tri-k&#x0101;&#x1e47;&#x1e0d;a-bh&#x0101;&#x1e63;ya</em>, n. <em>-pada</em> n. <em>-br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a</em> n. <em>-bh&#x0101;&#x1e63;ya</em> n. <em>-ma&#x00f1;jar&#x012b;</em> f. <em>-mantra-sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101;-sukha-bodhana</em> n. <em>-lak&#x1e63;a&#x1e47;a</em> n. <em>-&#x015b;&#x0101;kh&#x0101;</em> f. <em>-&#x015b;r&#x0101;ddha</em> n. <em>-&#x015b;rauta</em> n. <em>-sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101;</em> f. (and <em>&#x25cb;t&#x00e2;nukrama&#x1e47;ik&#x0101;</em> f. <em>&#x25cb;t&#x0101;br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;a</em> n.), <em>-sm&#x0101;rta</em>, n. ;<em>&#x25cb;d&#x00e2;ra&#x1e47;yaka</em> n. <em>&#x25cb;d&#x00e2;r&#x1e47;ava</em> m. <em>&#x25cb;d&#x00e2;&#x015b;&#x012b;r-v&#x0101;da</em> m. <em>&#x25cb;d&#x00f4;pani&#x1e63;ad</em> (?), f.            <dt>&#x226b; yad&#x0101; </dt>
           <dd><em>yad&#x0101;&#x0341;</em> ind. (fr. 3. <em>ya</em>) when, at what time, whenever (generally followed by the correlatives <em>tad&#x0101;</em>, <em>tatas</em>, <em>tarhi</em>, in Veda also by <em>&#x0101;&#x0341;t</em>, <em>&#x0101;&#x0341;d &#x012b;&#x0341;t</em>, <em>&#x00e1;tha</em>, <em>&#x00e1;dha</em> and <em>t&#x00e1;d</em>) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c. (<em>yad&#x0101; yad&#x0101;</em>, followed by <em>tad&#x0101;</em> or <em>tad&#x0101; tad&#x0101;</em>, 'as often as - so often', 'whenever' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad&#x0101;</em> - <em>tad&#x0101;</em> id., with repeated verbs, e.g. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Hit">Hit.</a> i, 197 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad&#x00e2;iva-tad&#x00e2;iva</em>, 'when indeed - then indeed' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;ak">&#x015a;ak.</a> <em>yad&#x0101; prabh&#x1e5b;ti</em> - <em>tad&#x0101; prabh&#x1e5b;ti</em>, 'from whatever time - from that time forward' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad&#x00e2;iva khalu</em> - <em>tad&#x0101; prabhrity eva</em>, 'as soon as - thence forward' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;ak">&#x015a;ak.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad&#x0101; kad&#x0101;&#x0341; ca</em>, 'as often as', 'whenever' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad&#x0101; kad&#x0101; cit</em>, 'at any time' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Kau&#x015b;">Kau&#x015b;.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad&#x0101; tad&#x0101;</em>, 'always' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Naish">Naish.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the copula after <em>yad&#x0101;</em> is often dropped, esp. after a participle, e.g. <em>yad&#x0101; k&#x1e63;aya&#x1e43; gata&#x1e43; sarvam</em>, 'when all had gone to ruin' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> <em>yad&#x0101;</em> is sometimes joined with other relatives used indefinitely, e.g. <em>yo'tti yasya yad&#x0101; m&#x0101;&#x1e43;sam</em>, 'when any one eats the flesh of any one' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Hit">Hit.</a>)</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; yad&#x0101;nik&#x0101;mam </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;nik&#x0101;&#x0341;mam</em> ind. when it pleases <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a></dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; yad&#x0101;v&#x0101;jad&#x0101;var&#x012b; </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;v&#x0101;ja-d&#x0101;var&#x012b;</em> f. pl. N. of a S&#x0101;man <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Pa&#x00f1;cavBr">Pa&#x00f1;cavBr.</a></dd>

</dd>

           <dt>yatkara </dt>
           <dd><em>yat-kara</em> <em>yat-k&#x0101;ma</em>, <em>yat-k&#x0101;ra&#x1e47;am</em> &amp;c. col. 3</dd>

           <dt>yatna </dt>
           <dd><em>yatna</em> <em>yatya</em>, p. 841, cols. 1 and 2</dd>

           <dt>yatha&#x1e5b;&#x1e63;i </dt>
           <dd><em>yatha-&#x1e5b;&#x1e63;i</em> <em>yatharcam</em> &amp;c. p. 841, col. 2</dd>

           <dt>yath&#x0101; </dt>
           <dd><em>yath&#x0101;</em> <em>yath&#x00e2;&#x1e43;&#x015b;a-tas</em> &amp;c. p. 841, cols. 2 and 3 &amp;c</dd>

           <dt>yad </dt>
           <dd><em>y&#x00e1;d</em> (nom. and acc. sg. n. and base in comp. of 3. <em>ya</em>), who, which, what, whichever, whatever, that <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c. (with correlatives <em>tad</em>, <em>tyad</em>, <em>etad</em>, <em>idam</em>, <em>adas</em>, <em>tad etad</em>, <em>etad tyad</em>, <em>ida&#x1e43; tad</em>, <em>tad idam</em>, <em>t&#x0101;d&#x1e5b;&#x015b;a</em>, <em>&#x012b;d&#x1e5b;&#x015b;a</em>, <em>&#x012b;d&#x1e5b;&#x015b;</em>, <em>et&#x0101;vad</em>, by which it is oftener followed than preceded </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; or the correl. is dropped, e.g. <em>yas tu n&#x00e2;rabhate karma k&#x1e63;ipram bhavati nirdravya&#x1e25;</em>, '<em>he</em> indeed who does not begin work soon becomes poor' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; or the rel. is dropped, e.g. <em>andhakam bhart&#x0101;ra&#x1e43; na tyajet s&#x0101; mah&#x0101;-sat&#x012b;</em>, 'she who does not desert a blind husband is a very faithful wife' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Vet">Vet.</a> <em>yad</em> is often repeated to express 'whoever', 'whatever', 'whichever', e.g. <em>yo ya&#x1e25;</em>, 'whatever man' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101; y&#x0101;</em>, 'whatever woman </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yo yaj jayati tasya tat</em>, 'whatever he wins <em>in war</em> belongs to him' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> vii, 96 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad yad vadati tad tad bhavati</em>, 'whatever he says is true', or the two relatives may be separated by <em>hi</em>, and are followed by the doubled or single correl. <em>tad</em> e.g. <em>upyate yad dhi yad b&#x012b;jam tat tad eva prarohati</em>, 'whatever seed is sown, that even comes forth' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> ix, 40 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; similar indefinite meanings are expressed by the relative joined with <em>tad</em> e.g. <em>yasmai tasmai</em>, 'to any one whatever', esp. in <em>yadv&#x0101; tadv&#x0101;</em>, 'anything whatever' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; or by <em>ya&#x1e25;</em> with <em>ka&#x015b;ca</em>, <em>ka&#x015b;cana</em>, <em>ka&#x015b;cit</em>, or [in later language, not in Manu] <em>ko'pi</em> e.g. <em>ya&#x1e25; ka&#x015b;cit</em>, 'whosoever' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;ni k&#x0101;ni ca mitr&#x0101;&#x1e47;i</em>, 'any friends whatsoever' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yena ken&#x00e2;py up&#x00e2;yena</em>, 'by any means whatsoever.' <em>yad</em> is joined with <em>tvad</em> to express generalization, e.g. <em>&#x015b;&#x016b;dr&#x0101;&#x1e43;s tvad y&#x0101;&#x1e43;s tvad</em>, 'either the &#x015a;&#x016b;dras or anybody else' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; or immediately followed by a pers. pron. on which it lays emphasis, e.g. <em>yo'ham</em>, 'I that very person who' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yas tva&#x1e43; katha&#x1e43; vettha</em>, 'how do you know?' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; it is also used in the sense of 'si quis', e.g. <em>striya&#x1e43; sp&#x1e5b;&#x015b;ed ya&#x1e25;</em>, 'should any one touch a woman.' <em>yad</em> is also used without the copula, e.g. <em>andho ja&#x1e0d;a&#x1e25; p&#x012b;&#x1e6d;ha sarp&#x012b; saptaty&#x0101; sthavira&#x015b;ca ya&#x1e25;</em>, 'a blind man, an idiot, a cripple, and a man seventy years old' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> viii, 394 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sometimes there is a change of construction in such cases, e.g. <em>ye ca m&#x0101;nu&#x1e63;&#x0101;&#x1e25;</em> for <em>m&#x0101;nu&#x1e63;&#x0101;&#x1e43;&#x015b;-ca</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> x, 86 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the nom. sg. n. <em>yad</em> is then often used without regard to gender or number and may be translated by 'as regards', 'as for', e.g. <em>k&#x1e63;atra&#x1e43; v&#x0101; etad vanaspat&#x012b;n&#x0101;&#x1e43; yan nyag-rodha&#x1e25;</em>, 'as for the Nyag-rodha, it is certainly the prince among trees' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AitBr">AitBr.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; or by 'that is to say', 'to wit', e.g. <em>tato dev&#x0101; eta&#x1e43; vajra&#x1e43; dad&#x1e5b;&#x015b;ur yad apa&#x1e25;</em>, 'the gods then saw this thunderbolt, to wit, the water' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> <em>yad</em> as an adv. conjunction generally = 'that', esp. after verbs of saying, thinking &amp;c., often introducing an oratio directa with or without <em>iti</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>iti yad</em>, at the end of a sentence = 'thinking that', 'under the impression that', e.g. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Ratn&#x00e2;v">Ratn&#x00e2;v.</a> ii, 2/8. <em>yad</em> also = 'so that', 'in order that', 'wherefore', 'whence', 'as', 'in as much as', 'since', 'because' [the correlative being <em>tad</em>, 'therefore'], 'when', 'if' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>&#x00e1;dha y&#x00e1;d</em>, 'even if', 'although' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <em>yad api</em> id. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Megh">Megh.</a> <em>yad u</em> - <em>evam</em>, 'as - so' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;vetUp">&#x015a;vetUp.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yad uta</em>, 'that' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#B&#x0101;lar">B&#x0101;lar.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; 'that is to say', 'scilicet' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#K&#x0101;ra&#x1e47;&#x1e0d;">K&#x0101;ra&#x1e47;&#x1e0d;.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Divy&#x00e2;v">Divy&#x00e2;v.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yat kila</em>, 'that' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Prasannar">Prasannar.</a> </dd>

           <dt>&#x226b; yadi </dt>
           <dd><em>y&#x00e1;di</em> ind. (in Veda also <em>y&#x00e1;d&#x012b;</em>, sometimes <em>yadi cit</em>, <em>yadi ha vai</em>, <em>y&#x00e1;d&#x012b;74t</em>, <em>y&#x00e1;dy u</em>, <em>yady u vai</em>) if, in case that <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c. In the earlier language <em>yadi</em> may be joined with Indic., Subj. or Le&#x1e6d;, Pot., or Fut., the consequent clause of the conditional sentence being generally without any particle. In the later language <em>yadi</em> may be joined with Pres. (followed in cons&#x1e6d;consequent clause by another Pres., e.g. <em>yadi j&#x012b;vati bhadr&#x0101;&#x1e47;i pa&#x015b;yati</em>, 'if he lives he beholds prosperity', or by fut. or by Impv. or by Pot. or by no verb) <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p845-1"></a>[Page 845, Column 1]</font>
 ; or it may be joined with Pot. (e.g. <em>yadi r&#x0101;j&#x0101; da&#x1e47;&#x1e0d;a&#x1e43; na pra&#x1e47;ayet</em>, 'if the king were not to inflict punishment', followed by another Pot. or by Cond. or by Pres. or by Impv. or by fut. or by no verb) ; or it may be joined with fut. (e.g. <em>yadi na kari&#x1e63;yanti tat</em>, 'if they will not do that', followed by another fut. or by Pres. or by Impv. or by no verb) ; or it may be joined with Cond. (e.g. <em>yady anuj&#x00f1;&#x0101;m ad&#x0101;syat</em>, 'if he should give permission', followed by another Cond. or by Pot. or by aor.) ; or it may be joined with aor. (e.g. <em>yadi praj&#x0101;-patir na vapur arsr&#x0101;k&#x1e63;&#x012b;t</em>, 'if the Creator had not created the body', followed by Cond. or by Pot. or by pf.) ; or it may be joined with Impv. or even with pf. (e.g. <em>yady &#x0101;ha</em>, 'if he had said'). There may be other constructions, and in the consequent clauses some one of the following may be used: <em>atha</em>, <em>atra</em>, <em>tad</em>, <em>tena</em>, <em>tatas</em>, <em>tata&#x1e25; param</em>, <em>tad&#x0101;</em>, <em>tarhi</em>, <em>tad&#x0101;n&#x012b;m</em>. Observe that <em>yadi</em> may sometimes = 'as sure as' (esp. in asseverations, followed by Impv. with or without <em>tath&#x0101;</em> or <em>tena</em> or followed by Pot. with <em>tad</em>) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#K&#x0101;v">K&#x0101;v.</a> &amp;c. ; or it may = 'whether' (followed by Pres. or Pot. or no verb, e.g. <em>yadi-na v&#x0101;</em>, 'whether-or not', and sometimes <em>kim</em> is added) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a> ; or it may = 'that' (after verbs of 'not believing' or 'doubting', with Pres. or Pot., e.g. <em>n&#x00e2;&#x015b;a&#x1e43;se yadi j&#x012b;vanti</em>, 'I do not expect that they are alive', <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#cf">cf.</a> P&#x0101;&#x1e47;. 3-3, 147 <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Sch">Sch.</a>) ; or if placed after <em>du&#x1e63;kara&#x1e43;</em> or <em>katha&#x1e43; cid</em> it may = 'hardly', 'scarcely' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> ; or it may = 'if perchance', 'perhaps' (with Pot. with or without <em>iti</em>, or with fut. or pres.) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#K&#x0101;v">K&#x0101;v.</a> &amp;c. The following are other combinations: - <em>yadi t&#x0101;vat</em>, 'how would it be if' (with Pres. or Impv.) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yadi n&#x0101;ma</em>, 'if ever' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yadi c&#x00ea;t</em> (<em>c&#x00ea;t</em> being added redundantly) = 'if' (e.g. <em>yadi c&#x00ea;t sy&#x0101;t</em>, 'if it should be') </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>pur&#x0101; yadi</em> = 'before' (e.g. <em>pur&#x0101; yadi pa&#x015b;y&#x0101;mi</em>, 'before that I see') </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x00e1;dy &#x00e1;pi</em> (rarely <em>api yadi</em>), 'even if', 'although' (followed by <em>tath&#x00e2;pi</em> or <em>tad api</em> or sometimes by no particle in the correlative clause) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yadi</em> - <em>yadi ca-yady api</em>, 'if - and if - if also' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x00e1;di</em> - <em>y&#x00e1;di-v&#x0101;</em>, or <em>y&#x00e1;di v&#x0101;</em> - <em>y&#x00e1;di v&#x0101;</em>, or <em>y&#x00e1;di v&#x0101;</em> - <em>y&#x00e1;di</em>, or <em>yadi v&#x0101;</em> - <em>v&#x0101;</em>, or <em>v&#x0101;</em> - <em>yadi v&#x0101;</em>, or <em>yad v&#x0101;</em> - <em>yadi v&#x0101;</em>, 'if - or if', 'whether - or' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x00e1;di v&#x0101;</em> - <em>n&#x00e1; v&#x0101;</em>, 'whether - or not' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>v&#x0101;</em> - <em>yadi v&#x0101;</em> - <em>yadi v&#x0101;-tath&#x00e2;pi</em>, 'whether - or - or - yet' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>v&#x0101; yadi</em> = 'or if', 'or rather' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yadi v&#x0101;</em> id. or = 'yet', 'however.'</dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; (in Yoga) self-restraint (as the first of the eight A&#x1e45;gas or means of attaining mental concentration) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#IW">IW.</a> 93 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; any rule or observance <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#P&#x0101;rG&#x1e5b;">P&#x0101;rG&#x1e5b;.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (<em>yam&#x00e1;</em>), mf(<em>&#x0101;&#x0341;</em> or <em>&#x012b;&#x0341;</em>)n. twin-born, twin, forming a pair <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; m. a twin, one of a pair or couple, a fellow (du. 'the twins', N. of the A&#x015b;vins and of their twin children by M&#x0101;dr&#x012b;, called Nakula and Saha-deva </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yamau mithunau</em>, twins of different sex) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#ib">ib.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; a symbolical N. for the number 'two' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Hcat">Hcat.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; N. of the god who presides over the Pit&#x1e5b;is (q.v.) and rules the spirits of the dead <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#IW">IW.</a> 18 ; 197, 198 &amp;c. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RTL">RTL.</a> 10 ; 16 ; 289 &amp;c. (he is regarded as the first of men and born from Vivasvat, 'the Sun', and his wife Sara&#x1e47;y&#x016b; </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; while his brother, the seventh Manu, another form of the first man, is the son of Vivasvat and Sa&#x1e43;j&#x00f1;&#x0101;, the image of Sara&#x1e47;y&#x016b; </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; his twin-sister is Yam&#x012b;, with whom he resists sexual alliance, but by whom he is mourned after his death, so that the gods, to make her forget her sorrow, create night </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the Veda he is called a king or <em>sa&#x1e43;gamano jan&#x0101;n&#x0101;m</em>, 'the gatherer of men', and rules over the departed fathers in heaven, the road to which is guarded by two broad-nosed, four-eyed, spotted dogs, the children of &#x015a;aram&#x0101;, q.v </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in Post-vedic mythology he is the appointed Judge and 'Restrainer' or 'Punisher' of the dead, in which capacity he is also called <em>dharmar&#x0101;ja</em> or <em>dharma</em> and corresponds to the Greek Pluto and to Minos </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; his abode is in some region of the lower world called Yama-pura </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; thither a soul when it leaves the body, is said to repair, and there, after the recorder, Citra-gupta, has read an account of its actions kept in a book called Agra-sa&#x1e43;dh&#x0101;n&#x0101;, it receives a just sentence </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> Yama is described as dressed in blood-red garments, with a glittering form, a crown on his head, glowing eyes and like Varu&#x1e47;a, holding a noose, with which he binds the spirit after drawing it from the body, in size about the measure of a man's thumb </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; he is otherwise represented as grim in aspect, green in colour, clothed in red, riding on a buffalo, and holding a club in one hind and noose in the other </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the later mythology he is always represented as a terrible deity inflicting tortures, called <em>y&#x0101;tan&#x0101;</em>, on departed spirits <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p846-2"></a>[Page 846, Column 2]</font> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; he is also one of the 8 guardians of the world as regent of the South quarter </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; he is the regent of the Nakshatra Apa-bharan&#x012b; or Bhara&#x1e47;&#x012b;, the supposed author of <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> x, 10 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; 14, of a hymn to Vish&#x1e47;u and of a law-book </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yamasy&#x00e2;rka&#x1e25;</em>, N. of a S&#x0101;man <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x0100;rshBr">&#x0100;rshBr.</a>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; N. of the planet Saturn (regarded as the son of Vivasvat and Ch&#x0101;y&#x0101;) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Hariv">Hariv.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BhP">BhP.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; of one of Skanda's attendants (mentioned together with Ati-yama) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> </dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; a bad horse (whose limbs are either too small or too large) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#L">L.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (<em>&#x012b;&#x0341;</em>), f. N. of Yama's twin-sister (who is identified in Postvedic mythology with the river-goddess Yamun&#x0101;) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; n. a pair, brace, couple <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#L">L.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (in gram.) a twin-letter (the consonant interposed and generally understood, but not written in practice, between a nasal immediately preceded by one of the four other consonants in each class) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Pr&#x0101;t">Pr&#x0101;t.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Pat">Pat.</a> on <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#P&#x0101;&#x1e47;">P&#x0101;&#x1e47;.</a> 1-1, 8 </dd>

           <dt>y&#x0101;vat </dt>
           <dd><em>y&#x0101;&#x0341;vat</em> mf(<em>at&#x012b;</em>)n. (fr. 3. <em>ya</em> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; correlative of <em>t&#x0101;vat</em>, q.v.) as great, as large, as much, as many, as often, as frequent, as far, as long, as old &amp;c. (or how great &amp;c. = quantus, quot or qualis) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c. (<em>y&#x0101;&#x0341;vanta&#x1e25; k&#x00ed;yanta&#x1e25;</em>, 'as many as' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#TBr">TBr.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;&#x0341;vad v&#x0101; y&#x0101;vad v&#x0101;</em>, 'as much as possible' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;vat t&#x0101;vat</em>, 'so much as', in alg. applied to the first unknown quantity [= x] or so much of the unknown as its co-efficient number </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in this sense also expressed by the first syllable <em>y&#x0101;</em>, <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#cf">cf.</a> IW. 182 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>iti y&#x0101;vat</em> in Comms. 'just so much', 'only so', 'that is to say', 'such is the explanation') </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; ind. as greatly as, as far as, as much or as many as </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; as often as, whenever </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; as long as, whilst </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; as soon as, the moment that, until that, till, until <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c. (in these senses used with either pres., Pot., fut., impf., or aor., or with the simple copula). <em>y&#x0101;vat</em> with the 1st sg. of pres., rarely of Pot., may denote an intended action and may be translated by 'meanwhile', 'just' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;&#x0341;vad y&#x0101;vad-t&#x0101;&#x0341;vat t&#x0101;vat</em>, 'as gradually as-so' <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;van na</em>, 'while not', 'before', 'till' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; 'if not', 'whether not' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>na y&#x0101;vatt&#x0101;vat</em>, 'scarcely-when', 'no sooner-than' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>na param</em>, or <em>na kevalam-y&#x0101;vat</em>, 'not only-but even.' Sometimes <em>y&#x0101;vat</em> is also used as a preposition with a prec. or following acc., or with a following abl., rarely dat., e.g. <em>m&#x0101;sam eka&#x1e43; y&#x0101;vat</em>, 'during one month' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>s&#x016b;ry&#x00f4;daya&#x1e43; y&#x0101;vat</em>, 'until sunrise' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>sarpa-vivara&#x1e43; y&#x0101;vat</em>, 'up to the serpent's hole' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;vad</em> or <em>y&#x0101;vad-&#x0101; sam&#x0101;pan&#x0101;t</em>, 'until the completion' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;vad garbhasya parip&#x0101;k&#x0101;ya</em>, 'until the maturity of the fetus.' Sometimes also with a nom. followed by <em>iti</em> e.g. <em>anta iti y&#x0101;vat</em>, 'as far as the end' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>pa&#x00f1;ca y&#x0101;vad iti</em>, 'up to five' </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; or with another ind. word, e.g. <em>adya y&#x0101;vat</em>, 'up to this day.' <em>y&#x0101;vat&#x0101;</em> ind. as far as, as long as <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x0100;past">&#x0100;past.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#R">R.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BhP">BhP.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; till, until (with Pot.) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#L&#x0101;&#x1e6d;y">L&#x0101;&#x1e6d;y.</a> (with <em>na</em>, as long as not, before <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BhP">BhP.</a>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; as soon as, the moment that <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Cat">Cat.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in as much as <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Pat">Pat.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;&#x0341;vati</em> ind. as long as, as far as &amp;c. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;Br">&#x015a;Br.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#TBr">TBr.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>y&#x0101;vati-t&#x0101;vati</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Da&#x015b;">Da&#x015b;.</a></dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; y&#x0101;vatkap&#x0101;lam </dt>
